the\nPioneer\n10/11\nVector\nHelium\nMagnetometer.\nAn exploded\nview\nof the\nsensor\nis shown\nin the\nfigure\nopposite.\nThe\nfeedback\ncoils\nare\nconstructed\non this\nconstruction\nshows\nthat\nall\nalignment\nand\nstability\nrequirements\ncan\nbe\nmet\nwith\nsubstantial\nmargins.\nAn external\nset\nof conventional\narrangement.\nThe\nfluxgate\ncores\nare\nexcited\nby a tuned\ndrive\ncircuit\nto provide\nhigh\nexcitation\nwith\nlow drive\nlosses.\nThe\nsecond\nharmonic\nsignal\nfrom\nthe\nsensor\nis the\ntriaxial\ncoils.\nThe\ncircuits\nare\nimplemented\nusing\nmodern\noperational\namplifiers\nto provide\nthe\nrequired\nstability.\nThe\ncritical\ncurrent\nfeedback\ncomponents\nmust\nbe feedback\ncoil\naround\nthe\nsensor\nso that\nthe\nsensor\noperates\nin a null\nmode.\nThen,\nonly\nthe\nsensor\nnoise\nand\noffset\nmatter.\nIn our\nanalysis,\nwe eliminated\n\nby\n\nthemselves\nnulling\n\n-all\n\nthree\ncomponents\nof the\nvector\nfield\nat each\nsensor.\nMathematically,\nthis\nfinding\nrelates\nto the\nfact\nthat\nthe\norientation\nof a null\nvector\n(of zero\nlength)\nneed\nnot be specified.\nThus,\nour\nspecific\ndesign\napproach\nconsists\nof a system\nin which\nthree\northogonal\nsensors\nare\nsurrounded\nby three\northogonal\nfeedback\ncoils.\nIn investigating\nthis\nsystem,\nwe found\nthat\nthe\nexternal\nfield\ncan\nbe\ncancelled\nalmost\nexactly\n(to<0.0Z\nTat\n60 cm)\nby use\nof external\ncancellation\ncoils.\nBy careful\nselection\nof the\ncoil\ngeometry\nand the use\nof a\nsimple,\nrigid\nstructure\nusing\nisotropic\ngraphite-epoxy\nmaterials,\nas well\nas by providing\nthermal\nshielding,\nwe were\nable\nto obtain\nan estimated\nscale\nfactor\nand\nalignment\nstability\nof 1.5T\nand\n<5 seconds\nof arc,\nrespectively.\nThe\nweight\nand power\nrequirements\nof the\nsensor\nare\nlow:\n1.82\nkg\nand\n300 roW,\nthe power\nbeing\nalmost\nentirely\nthat\nof the\nthermal\ncontrol\nheater.\nThe\nfeedback\ncoil\nand\nsensor\ndrive\npower\nis only\n35 mW\nmaximum.\nElectronic\nDesign\nStudy\n- Because\nlow\nsensor\npower\ninput\nis required\nfor thermal\nstability\nof the\nsensor\nhousing,\na reactive\ndrive\nscheme\nis\nneeded\nto eliminate\nthe\nlosses\nproduced\nby conventional\ncurrent\nor voltage\ndrive\nmethods.\nExcept\nfor the\nuse\nof this\ntechnique\n(to be flown\non MJS)\nthe\nsensor\ndrive\nand\nac signal\nhandling\ncircuits\ncan be conventional.\nThe\nimportant\nproblem\nis the\ndesign\nof the\nfeedback\nsystem\nand the\nADC.\nThe\nstudy\nfound\nthat\neither\na single-range\nADC\nor a limited-range\nADC\nwith\nseveral\noffset\nranges\ncould\nmeet\nthe\nrequirements;\nthe\ndesign\napproach\nstudied\nin detail\nwas\nbased\non the\nmultiple-range\nconfiguration.\nTo achieve\nthe\nnecessary\nstability\nof the\nfeedback\ncoil\ncurrent,\nit is\nnecessary\n\xc2\xb15\xc2\xb0C.\n\ni-8\n\nto\n\ncontrol\n\nthe\n\ntemperature\n\nof\n\nthe\n\nfeedback\n\ncurrent\n\nsource\n\nto\n\n3\n\nTIME\n\n(\n\n-ZERO\n\nCalibration\nStudy\n- Magnetometer\n\nCOMPONENTS\n\nOF\n\nTHE\n\nDesign\n\nVECTOR\n\nRequirements\n\nMAGNETOMETER\n\nA vector\nfluxgate magnetometer\nhas three separate\nsensor\nchannels,\none\nfor each axis.\nThe characteristics\nof the sensor,\nsignal electronics,\nfeedback\ncircuits,\nand digitizing circuits must\nbe appropriately\nselected\nto meet\nthe overall performance\nrequirements.\nTo design\nthe\nVector\nMagnetometer,\nit is necessary\nto translate\nthe\noverall\nperformance\nrequirements\njust\ndescribed\ninto\ndesign\nrequirements\nfor\neach\ncomponent\nof the\nmagnetometer.\nThe\nrequirements\nfor\nMAGSAT\ncan be met\nby use\nof either\na vector\nhelium\nor a three-axis\nfluxgate\nmagnetometer.\nThe\nvector\nhelium\nmagnetometer\nprovides\nbetter\nlow-frequency\nnoise\nperformance\nat the\ncost\nof\ngreater\ncomplexity;\nbecause\nthis\nparticular\nlow-noise\ncharacteristic\nis not\nneeded\nfor\nthe\nMAGSAT\napplication,\na fluxgate\nmagnetometer\nhas\nbeen\nselected\nfor\nstudy.\nThe\ncomponents\nwhich\ntypically\nmake\nup a fluxgate\nmagnetometer\nare\nshown\nopposite,\nfor\none\nof three\nsensor\nchannels;\nthe\ncentral\npower\nsupply,\nsequencing\nlogic,\nand\nother\nhousekeeping\nand\nsupport\nsystems\nare\nnot shown.\nHow\nthe\nFluxgate\nOperates\n- The\nfluxgate\nsensor\nconsists\nof a magnetic\ncore\nconsisting\nof either\na pair\nof long\nrods\nor a tape-wound\ntoroid\nof a\nhigh\npermeability\nsquare-loop\ncore\nmaterial.\nIt is driven\ninto\nsaturation\nat a high\naudio\nfrequency\n(typically\n10 kHz)\nby current\nin a drive\nwinding.\nIn the\npresence\nof an external\nfield,\nan even-harmonic\nflux\nchange\nis generated\nin the\ncore\nas a result\nof a variation\nin the\nsaturation\ntime\nof the\ndifferent\nparts\nof the\ncore.\nThis\nsignal\nis amplified,\nsynchronously\ndemodulated,\nfiltered,\nand fed back\nas a current\ninput\nto a feedback\ncoil\nwhich\nproduces\na field\nto null\nthe\nexternal\nfield.\nThe\nsensor\nthen\nfunctions\nonly\nas a null-sensing\ndevice\nand does\nnot have\nto meet\nhigh\nlinearity\nor gain\nstability\nrequirements.\nThe\nsignal\nwhich\ndrives\nthe\nfeedback\ncoil\nis digitized\nto provide\nthe\noutput\ndata\nwhich\nis a number\ndirectly\nrelated\nto the\nvalue\nof the\nexternal\nfield.\nthe\n\nTo implement\norganization\n\nthe\nblock\ndiagram\nand performance\n\nshown,\ncharacteristics\n\nit\n\nis\n\nnecessary\nfor\neach\n\nto decide\nblock.\n\non\n\nOrganization\nof the\nFeedback\nArrangement\n- The\nfield\nalong\neach\naxis\nof the magnetometer\nis measured\nby a separate\nsensor\nwith\nseparate\nelectronics\nas shown.\nOften,\nthe\nsensors\nfor each\naxis\nare\nphysically\nseparated,\nand use\none\ncoil\nboth\nto sense\nthe\nsignal\nand\nto provide\nfeedback\nto cancel\none\ncomponent\nof the\napplied\nfield.\nAlternatively,\na set\nof orthogonal\ncoils\ncan\nbe used\nto null\nthe field\nover\nan entire\nvolume\noccupied\nby\nthree\nsensors.\nIn either\ncase,\nthe\nthree\nsensor\nelectronics\nchannels\nfunction\nindependently\nand\nhave\nthe\nsame\nblock\ndiagram;\nbut it is necessary\nto\nselect\nthe feedback\narrangement\nwhich\nprovides\nthe\nbest\nperformance.\nOrsanization\nof the Digitizing\nSystem\n- For some\napplications\nthe\ndynamic\nrange\nof the applied field is very large.\nFor MAGSAT,\nthe ratio\nof the total field variation\nto the quantizing\ninterval is I28000Y/IY,\nor\nslightly less than 217 . Covering\nsuch a wide dynamic\nrange with one\nanalog-to-digital\nconverter\ncan be avoided\nby using a sampling\nconversion\nwithin the feedback\nloop or by offsetting the feedback\ncurrent\nby a switched\nconstant\ncurrent\nto optimize\nthe overall digitizer performance.\nThe selection of the appropriate\ndigitizing scheme\nis another\nquestion\nto be decided.\nIn addition to these two organizational\nquestions\n(considered\nin detail\nin the remainder\nof this report),\none must\nspecify the performance\nrequirements\nfor each component\nof the magnetometer.\nThis allocation\nof use\n\nDesign\n\n)\n\nREQUIREMENTS\ncan be met\nby the use\nof sensor\nfeedback\ncircuits\nand\ncoils.\nBoth\nsensor\nand\neleccontrol;\nlow thermal\ngradients\nin the\nof superinsulation\nand low\ncoil\npower.\n\nMagnetometers\nwith\noffset\nand\nnoise\nperformance\nequal\nto that\nrequired\nhave\nbeen\npreviously\nflown,\nbut the\nrequirements\nfor absolute\naccuracy\nand\nalignment\npresent\nnew problems.\nThe\nfollowing\nqualitative\ndiscussion\nindicates\nwhat\ndesign\napproaches\nare\nnecessary\nto meet\nthe\nperformance\nrequirements.\nGain\nStability\nand\nLinearity\n- The\naccurate\nmeasurement\nof the\nfield\nalong\neach\naxis\nof the\nmagnetometer\nrequires\nvery\nhigh\ngain\nand\noffset\nstability\nand linearity.\nTo achieve\nthe\nrequired\ngain\nstability\nand\nlinearity,\nthe magnetic\nfield\nsensors\n(of whatever\nkind)\nmust\nbe enclosed\nin feedback\ncoils\nso that\nthe\nsensor\noperates\nonly\nas a null\ndetector.\nSince\nthe\nfield\nproduced\nby a coil\nis a function\nof its\nsize,\nthermal\nexpansion\nof the\ncoil\nbecomes\na critical\nmatter,\nrequiring\ntemperature\ncontrol\nof the\nsensors\nas well\nas the\nUse of thermally\nstable\nmaterials.\nTo generate\nthe\nfeedback\nfield,\nthe\nfeedback\ncoils\nmust\nbe driven\nby aprecision\ncurrent\nsource\nwhose\noutput\nimpedance\nis much\nhigher\nthan\nthe unstable\ncoil\nimpedance.\nThe\noverall\nloop\ngain\nmust\nbe high.\nOffset\nStability\n- The\nattainment\nof the\nrequired\noffset\nstability\nrequires\nlow\noffsets\nin the\nsensor,\nthe\nac drive\nand\nsignal\ncircuits,\nthe\ndc feedback\nsystem,\noffset\n\nand the\nstabilities\n\nanalog-to-digital\nconverter\n(ADC).\nand\nnoise\nperformance\ncomparable\n\nFluxgate\nto these\n\nsensors\nrequired\n\nwith\nhave\n\nbeen\nbuilt\nby Time-Zero\nLaboratories\nand\nothers\nusing\ncore\nmaterials\nlow\nmagnetostriction.\nThe\nrecommended\nsensors\nuse\nthe\n6-81.3\nMoPermalloy\nrecommended\nby the\nNaval\nOrdnance\nLaboratory.\nThe\nelectronic\noffsets\narise\nfrom\nseveral\nsources,\nnamely,\ngeneration\nof second\nharmonic\nsignals\nin the\nin the\ndemodulator-filter,\n\ndrive\ncircuit\nand\ncurrent\nsource,\n\nsignal\nand\n\namplifiers,\nADC.\nThese\n\nwith\n\nand dc offsets\ncan\nbe con-\n\ntrolled\n\nby the precautions\nindicated\nin the table.\nAxis\nStability\n- Attainment\nof the\nrequired\naxis\nstability\nrequires\nstability\nof the\nsensor\nmounting\nstructure\nand\ninternal\norientation.\nTo\nachieve\nsuch\nstability,\nthe\nsensor\nsubsystem\nmust\nbe kept\nat a constant\ntemperature\nand must\nbe designed\nfor low thermal\ngradients\nin the\nstructure,\nwhich\nin turn\nimplies\nminimum\npower\ninput\nto the\nsensor.\nTo avoid\nthermoelectric\nor induced\ncurrents,\nthe\nsensor\nhousing\nmust\nbe made\nof\nrelatively\nnon-conducting\nmaterials\nwhich\npossess\nsufficient\nthermal\nstability\nto stay\nin alignment\nin spite\nof the\ninternal\nthermal\ngradients\nproduced\nby the\nsensor.\nFinally,\nit is important\nto arrange\nthe\nfeedback\nso\nthat\nthe\nalignment\ndepends\nonly\non the\nfeedback\ncoil\ngeometry.\nThe\nconventional\nsingle-axis\nfluxgate\nsensor\nis feedback-stabilized\nalong\nonly\none\naxis.\nMotion\nof the\nsensitive\nmagnetic\nelement\nnormal\nto this\naxis\nproduces\na first-order\nmisalignment\nerror\nfor fields\nnormal\nto the\nfeedback\naxis,\neven\nif the\norientation\nof the feedback\nand pickup\ncoil\nis stable.\nThis\ndifficulty\ncan be circumvented\nby enclosing\nall three\nsensors\nin\na single\nvolume\nin which\nthe\nvector\nfield\nis nulled,\nrather\nthan\nnulling\nthe\nthree\ncomponents-separately\nat different\nlocations.\nThe\nonly\ncritical\nassembly\nis now the\nfeedback\ncoil\nstructure\n-- which\nis less\ncritical\nthan\nfor\na single-axis\nsystem\nbecause\nthere\nare\nfewer\nparameters\nto be controlled\nand\nthe\nstructural\nand\nthermal\ndesign\nis easier.\nThe\nexternal\nfield\n\n3-Z\n\n)\n\nTIME\nis larger,\ncoils.\n\nbut\n\nvery\n\nlow\n\nexternal\n\nfields\n\ncan\n\nbe\n\nattained\n\nby\n\n* ZEI:IO\n\nthe\n\nuse\n\nof\n\ncorrection\n\nStability\nof the sensor\nalone\nis of no use\nunless\nthe location\nof the axes\ncan\nbe determined\nboth\nin flight\nand during\ncalibration.\nThe transfer\nbetween\nthe\nsensor\ncoordinate\nsystem\nand the coordinate\nsystem\nof the\noptical\nreference\nmirrors\nmust\nbe stable\nas well,\nimplying\nthe use\nof a thermal\ndesign\nwhich\nminimizes\nthermal\ngradients.\nAxis\nDetermination\n- To calibrate\nthe axis\ndetermination\nsystem,\nit is\nnecessary\nto produce\na magnetic\nfield\nwhose\ndirection\nis known\nwith\nthe\nrequired\naccuracy.\nThis\nproblem\nis as difficult\nas the design\nof the\nsensor,\nbut the facilities\nare to be made\navailable\nat the Goddard\nSpace\nFlight\nCenter.\nIt seems\nclear\nthe final\ncalibration\nshould\nbe clone\nwith\nthe actual\noptical\nsystem\nto be used\nin flight,\nso there\nwill\nbe no inaccuracies\nresulting\nfrom\ncros s - calibrations.\nThis\ndiscussion\nindicates\nthat\nspecial\ncare\nmust\nbe taken\nin designing\nthe\nsensor\nstructure\nand in assuring\nthat\nthe sensor\nis stable\nin the\nrange\nof\nflight\nenvironments\nto be expected.\nThe\noffset\nrequirements\nare\nsimilar\nto\nthose\nof instruments\npreviously\nflown;\nthe gain\nand its\nlogic\ncontroller.\nThe\nentire\nprocess\noperates\nsynchronously\nwith\nsignals\nfrom\nthe\nspacecraft.\nThe\ncritical\nproblems\nin the\ndesign\nof this\nsystem\nare\nthe\nmechanical\nand Design\nPHYSICAL AND INTERFACE CHARACTERISTICS FOR THE\nRECOMMENDED SENSOR DESIGN\nThe recommended triaxial feedback sensor is located at the end of a boom\nin a thermal enclosure mounted on a thermally shielded base plate carrying the alignment mirrors.\nThe electronics package is mounted in the\nspacecraft and communicates with the sensor by means of a boom cable.\nThe weight and power requirements are less than specified.\nHere we briefly summarize the physical and interface characteristics\nof the design. The vector\nmagnetometer\nsensor\nhas\nbeen\ndesigned\nunder\nthe\nassumption\nthat\nit will\nnetometer\nsensor\nmounted\n\nbe carried\nnot closer\n\non the\nsame\nboom\nas a scaler\nthan\nZ4 inches\naway\n(center-to-\n\nmag-\n\ncenter}.\nThe\nenvelope,\nweight,\nand\npower\nconsumption\ncharacteristics\nare\nsummarized\nin the\ntable\nopposite.\nIn general,\nwe have\ntried\nto achieve\nthe\nminimum\nweight\nby making\nthe\nsensor\nas small\nas possible\nconsistent\nwith\nmeeting\nthe\nmodified\nnoise\nspecification.\n(The\nnoise\ndetermines\nthe\nsize\nbecause\nbigger\nfluxgate\nsensors\nhave\nlower\nnoise,\nand the\nsize\nof the\nsensors\ndirectly\nimpacts\nthe\nsize\nof the\nfeedback\ncoils\nand\nsurrounding\nstructural\nand thermal\nshield.)\nThe power\nis kept\nas low\nas possible,\nand the\nsolar\nheating\nhas\nbeen\nreduced\nbyuse\nof a low-absorptive\nfinish.\nThis\napproach\nnot only\nreduces\ngradients\nbut minimizes\nthe\ndifference\nbetween\nthe\nsolar\ninsolation\nand eclipse\nconditions.\nThe\nheater\nsize\nhas\nbeen\nchosen\nto compensate\nfor the\nlosses\nthrough\nthe\nsuperinsulations\nand\nfrom\nthe\nsurface\nof the\nalignment\nmirrors.\nElectronics\n- Configuration\nOF\n\nOPTIMUM\n\nAnalysis\nSENSOR\n\nCONFIGURATION\n\nTo meet\nthe alignment\nstability\nrequirement\nsor\nshould\nemploy\ntriaxial\nvector\nfeedback.\nadequate\nfield\nuniformity,\nespecially\nif the\nfied.\nA concentric\nlarger\nset\nof Helmholtz\nplete\ncancellation\nof the\nexternal\nfield.\n\nANALYSIS\n\nin an optimum\nway,\nthe\nsenHelmholtz\ncoil\npairs\nproduce\ncoil\nspacing\nis slightly\nmodicoils\nwill\nprovide\nalmost\ncom-\n\nBefore\nplunging\ninto\nthe details\nof a specific\nsensor\ndesign\nand\nperformance\nanalysis,\nwe will\npresent\nthe\nanalysis\nwhich\nled to the\nselection\nof the\ndesign.\nIn the\nfollowing\npages,\nthe\nrationale\nfor\na design\noptimized\nfor\nalignment\nstability\nis fully\ndeveloped;\nhere,\nwe summarize\nthe\nanalysis\nbriefly.\nSelection\nof Feedback\nConfiguration\n- To provide\nthe required\nstability\nand linearity,\nthe fluxgate\nsensors\nused\nmust\nbe used\nin the null\nmode.\nThe earth\'s\nfield\nis cancelled\nby a feedback\nfield\nproduced\nby coils\nwhose\ncoil\nconstant\nand\nalignment\nmust\nbe stable.\nThere\nare\nat least\ntwo ways\nto organize\nthe feedback.\nEach\northogonal\nfluxgate\nsensor\ncan have\nits\nown feedback\ncoil-a single-axis\nsystem-or three\nfluxgates\ncan\nbe\nlocated\ninside\nthree\northogonal\nfeedback\ncoils\nwhich\nprovide\na vector\nfeedback\nfield.\nWe call\nthis\nsystem\ntriaxial\nfeedback.\nThe\nanalysis\npresented\nin this\nsubsection\nshows\nthat\nthe\nsensitivity\nto\nmisalignment\nof the fluxgate\nsensors\nis far less\nif triaxial\nfeedback\nis\nused,\nnot only\nbecause\nthe feedback\nloop\nis closed\nin all three\ndimensions\nfor each\nsensor,\nbut also\nbecause\nof a simpler\nmechanical\nconfiguration.\nBecause\nalignment\nstability\nis the most\ncritical\nrequirement\nfor the\nMAGSAT\nVector\nMagnetometer,\nthe triaxial\nfeedback\nsystem\nwas\nselected.\nFluxgate\nSensor\nConfiguration\n- The\nnoise\nof a fluxgate\nsensor\ndepends\non its\nsize\nand shape;\nthe\nsensors\ncan\nbe designed\nto attain\na specified\nnoise\nlevel.\nAccordingly,\nwe have\nselected\na sensor\nsize\nwhich\nis compatible\nwith\na modified\nnoise\nlevel\nrequirement\nof 1_ peak,\nselecting\nthe\ndiameter-to-height\nratio\nto give\na minimum\npackage\nsize\nfor the three\northogonal\nsensors\nmounted\nat the center\nof the triaxial\nfeedback\nfield.\nFeedback\nCoil\nConfiguration\n- The\nthree\nsensors\ncannot\nbe all\nat\nexactly\nthe same\nplace\nin the feedback\nfield.\nThe\nfield\ntherefore\nmust\nmeet\ncertain\nuniformity\nrequirements\nso that\nerrors\ndo not arise\nfrom\ninstabilities\nof the\nsensor\nposition\nor orientation.\nAttainment\nof a sufficiently\nuniform\nfield\nis simply\na matter\nof using\nan appropriate\nnumber\nof feedback\ncoils.\nThe\nproblem\nis to attain\nadequate\nuniformity\nwith\ncoils\nof minimum\nsize,\nweight\nand\ncomplexity.\nIn\nprinciple,\nthe use\nof many\ncoils\nallows\nthe use\nof very\nsmall\ncoils;\nbut,\nin practice,\nthe mechanical\ndesign\nto avoid\ninterferences\nbetween\ncoils\nprevents\nthe coil\nsystem\nfrom\nbeing\nvery\nsmall.\nAnalysis\nshows\nthat\nadequate\nfield\nuniformity\nis attained\nwith\na single\npair\nof coils\nper\naxis,\nwith\na coil\nspacing\nslightly\nless\nthan\ntheir\nradius\n(modified\nHelmholtz\nconfiguration).\nCancellation\nof External\nField\n- Because\nthe\nleading\nterm\nin the\nexternal\nfield\nis a dipole\nfield,\nthe external\nfield\ncan\nbe greatly\nreduced\nby cancelling\nthe dipole\nmoment\nof the main\nfeedback\ncoils\nwith\nan outer\npair\nof coils.\nBecause\nHelmholtz\ncoils\nhave\nno guadrupole\nfield,\nthe\nouter\ncoils\nshould\nalso\nbe Helmholtz\ncoils.\nLess\npower\nis required\nif\nthe coils\nare\nlarge\n-- at least\ntwice\nthe\nsize\nof the inner\ncoils.\n\n4-2\n\n)\n\nTIME*\n\nC\n\nZEFI\xc2\xa32\n\nModification\nof the\nField\n- A pair\nof Helmholtz\ncoils\nwith\na spacing\nequal\nto their\nradius\nproduces\na field\nflat\non the\naxis\nmidway\nbetween\nthe\ncoils.\nBecause\nthe\nfluxgate\nsensors\nare\noffset\nfrom\nthis\ncentral\nposition,\nit would\nbe better\nif the field\nwere\nflat\nat the\nsensor.\nThe\nradial\nposition\nof the\nflat\nspot\ncan\nbe put\nat the\noffset\nsensor\nposition\nby pushing\nthe\ncoils\ntogether\nslightly.\nDoing\nthis\nallows\nthe\nuse\nof minimum-size\nfeedback\ncoils.\nStructural\nand\nThermal\nDesign\nRequirements\n- From\nthe\nequation\nfield,\none\ncan obtain\nthe\nsensitivity\nof the field\nto various\ndimensional\nThe\nvalues\nof the\nsensitivity\nparameters\nhave\nbeen\nderived\nto specify\ntolerances\nrequired\nin the\nstructural\nand thermaldesign.\nThese\nmatters\nare\ntreated\nin detail\nin the\nfollowing\npages\nof this\nsubsection.\n\nTABLE\n\n4-I.\n\nSENSOR\n\nCONFIGURATION\n\nThe optimum\nconfiguration\nto the rationale\nindicated.\n\nANALYSIS\n\nof the sensor\n\nwas\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2 Triaxial\n\nfluxgate\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2 Helmholtz\n\ninner\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2 Large\nouter\nCancellation\n\n- Low\nmisalignment\n- Specific\n\nSUMMARY\n\nselected\n\nSelection\n\nfor\nthe\nchanges.\nthe\n\nmoment.\n\nmoment\n\nof\n\nquadrupole\nfiat\nrequired\n\nat\n\ninner\n\nmoment,\n\nsensor.\ncoil\n\nsize.\n\n(\n4-3\n\nSection\n4 - Sensor\nDesign\nSubsection\n4. 1 - Configuration\nDEPENDENCE\nMISALIGNMENT\n\nOF\n\nSENSOR\nSENSITIVITY\n\nAnalysis\nAND\n\nFEEDBACK\n\nCONFIGURATIONS\n\nON\n\nTo select the most\npromising\nsensor\nconfiguration\nfor the Vector\nMagnetometer,\nit is necessary\nto use one of the three fluxgate geometries-parallel-rod,\nracetrack,\nor ring-core-in a feedback\ncoil system\nwhich\nassures\nlow sensitivity to sensor\nmisalignment.\nFluxgate\nSensor\nCharacteristics\n- The fluxgate sensor\nis a remarkable device,\ncapable\nof measurement\nof magnetic\nfields over a very wide\ndynamic\nrange.\nFluxgates\nhave been flown to the moon\nand to all of the\ninner planets\nand Jupiter,\nand a fluxgate instrument\nis now en route to\nSaturn\non Pioneer\n11. Others\nwill fly on the MJS\n(Mars-Jupiter-Saturn)\nspacecraft.\nThe fluxgate is basically\na transformer\nwith a square\nloop core so that\nit acts as a magnetic\namplifier.\nThe flux is made\nto saturate\nalternately\nin each direction\nby an alternating\ncurrent\nin an ac drive winding.\nIn the\npresence\nof an external\nfield, a flux change\nat twice the drive frequency\nis\ngenerated\nin the core.\nThis flux change\ncan be detected\nby a sense winding\nand amplified\nto obtain a measure\nof the applied field.\nThe sense\nwinding\nis wound\ndifferentially to reject the drive; in practice,\nthis means\nthat the\nsense\nwinding\nis simply\nwrapped\naround\nthe core.\nThe noise is essentially\nBarkhausen\nnoise, while the offset appears\nto be produced\nby magnetostriction.\nThe two effects are related:\nmaterials\nwith low magnetostriction\nhave low noise as well.\nThe theory\nof the signal generation,\nnoise,\nand\noffset is discussed\nin detail in Appendix\nA.\nSeveral\ndifferent core configurations\nare possible-a pair of straight\nrods,\nan elongated\n(racetrack)\ntoroid,\nor a cylindrical\nring core.\nHistorically,\nthe racetrack\nsensor\nevolved\nfrom\nthe parallel\nrod sensor,\nwhile the ring core evolved\nfrom\nthe magnetic\namplifier,\nbeing simpler\nto\nmanufacture\nbecause\nof its cylindrical\nshape.\nThe principle\nof operation\nis the same\nfor all three.\nSelection\nof the fluxgate geometry\ndepends\non\nthe characteristics\nof the feedback\ncoil system.\nFeedback\nCharacteristics\n- The important\naspect\nof the sensor\ndesign\napproach\nis not so much\nthe selection\nof the type of fluxgate to be used,\nbut\nthe way the fluxgate is used in an overall feedback\nloop.\nFeedback\nmust\nbe used to generate\na magnetic\nfield which\nnulls the ambient\nfield to attain\nthe required\nlinearity and insensitivity\nto misalignment\nerror.\nIn this\nmanner\nthe sensor\nis used only as a null detector,\nso that the stability of\nits gain and linearity are not important.\nSuch feedback\nis commonly\nused\nin flight magnetometers\nfor precision\nmeasurements.\nTo minimize\nthe effects of sensor\nmisalignment,\nit is important\nto\norganize\nthis feedback\nin the proper\nway.\nHistorically,\nvector magnetometers have often been made\nby placing three single-axis\nfluxgates-either\nparallel-rod,\nracetrack,\nor ring-core-at right angles,\nwith a separate\nfeedback\ncoil for each sensor,\nas shown\nin Figure\n4-I.\nThe Pioneer\n10/ll\nVector\nHelium\nMagnetometer,\nbuilt for JPL\nby Time-Zero,\nis an exception:\nsince the helium-gas\nsensor\nis inherently\na vector\ndevice,\nthe feedback was accomplished\nby a set of three Helmholtz\ncoil pairs which\nproduced\na vector feedback\nfield (see Figure\n4-2).\nRing cores\nappear\nto be\nthe best kind of fluxgate sensor\nfor this triaxial configuration\nbecause\nthey\nallow a more\ncompact\nstructure,\nmaking\nit easier\nto produce\na feedback\nfield uniform\nover the sensor\nvolume.\n\n4-4\n\n)\n\nl\np\n\nTIIVIE\n\n- ZEFIO\n\nL\n\nMisalignment\nSensitivity\n- Comparing\nFigures\n4-1 and 4-2,\none might\nexpect\nthe single-axis\nand triaxial-feedback\narrangements\nto have\ndifferent\nsensitivities\nto sensor\nand structural\nmisalignment.\nFor example,\nthe singleaxis\nsensors\nare mounted\napart\nfrom\none another\non an extended\nstructure\nto\navoid\nsensor\ncrosstalk,\nwhile\nin the triaxial\ngeometry\nthe sensors\ncan be\nmounted\nin a compact\nassembly.\nBecause\nof the stringency\nof the alignment\nrequirement,\nthe configuration\nwhich\nhas the lowest\nsensitivity\nto rnisalignment\nerrors\nmust\nbe selected\nfor A4AGSAT.\nThe selection\nof the most\npromising\ngeometry\nthus requires\nan analysis\nof the misalignment\nsensitivity\nof\neach\nconfiguration.\nThis\nanalysis,\nwhich\nleads\nto the conclusion\nthat the triaxial\nconfiguration\nis far less\nsensitive\nto misalignment\nerror,\nis reported\nin the following\ntopics.\n\nt\n!\n\n_t\n\nNAS\n\n6-231Mll/4-1\n\nSINGLE-AXIS\nFLUXGATES\n\nX\n\nFigure\n4-1.\nSingle-Axis\nVector\nMagnetometer\nEach fluxgate\nsensor\nis surrounded\nby an the\nearth\'s\ngravitational\nfield\nas a result\nof its\nown\nweight\nor that\nof the\nsensors,\nthermal\nshielding,\nor mirrors.\nSensor\nStructure\nAlignment\n- The\nstructure\non which\nthe\nsensor\nfeedback\ncoils\nthemselves\nare\nmounted\nmust\nbe structurally\nand thermally\nstable,\nbecause\nthis\nstructure\ndefines\nthe\nrelationship\nbetween\nthe\nsensor\naxes\nand the\naxes\ndefined\nby the mirrors\nand their\nmounting\nplate.\nFor\na\nsingle-axis\nsystem,\nthe\nsensors\nare\nwell-separated\nso that\nthe\nfields\nof\ntheir\nindependent\nfeedback\ncoils\ndo not interact.\nFor\nsuch\nan arrangement,\nthe\nstability\nof the\nintervening\nstructure\nis particularly\ncritical.\nFor\nthe\ntriaxial\narrangement,\nthe\nsensors\nare\ncloser\ntogether,\nbut the\nfeedback\ncoil\nsystem\nis larger,\nso that\nclose\nattention\nis required\nto make\nthe\nmechanical\nand thermal\nfeedback\ncoil\nstructure\nrigid.\nThe\nstructural\nrigidity\nrequirement\nappears\nto be easier\nto meet\nfor the\nhighly\nsymmetrical\ntriaxial\narrangement\ncompared\nto the\nextended\nrod\nor plate\nstructures\nused\nfor\nsingle-axis\nmagnetometers\nwe know\nabout.\nFeedback\nCoil\nAlignment\n- The\norientation\nof the\nfeedback\ncoils\nis\nevidently\ncritical\nfor either\nsensor\ngeometry.\nThe\ncoils,\nwhich\nare\nwound\non forms\nand potted,\nmust\nbe designed\nto maintain\nthe\nrequired\nalignment\nstability\nrelative\nto the\nmounting\nstructure.\nTo achieve\na stability\nof\n5 seconds\nof arc\nrequires\na mechanical\nstability\nof ?5 microinches\nper\ninch.\nThis\nis of the\nsame\norder\nas the\nstability\nrequired\nof precision\noptical\nsystems.\nIt appears\neasier\nto define\nthe coil\norientation\nin the\ntriaxial\narrangement,\nbecause\nit is larger;\nif the\nstructure\nis rigid,\na\nsmall\nmotion\nof the\neffective\ncoil\naxis\nleads\nto a relatively\nsmaller\nangular\nmisalignment\nthan\ndoes\nthe\nsame\nlinear\nmotion\nof the\nrelatively\nsmall\nfeedback\ncoil\nused\nin the\nsingle-axis\nsensors.\n\n4-6\n\n]\n\nTIME\n\nGuaranteeing\nthe\nrelative\nalignment\nof the optical\ncoils\nis a matter\nof adequate\nstructural\nand thermal\nfeedback\nconfiguration\nis using a triaxial sensor\nwithin a triaxial feedback\ncoil, the sensitivity to\nsensor\nmisalignments\nis greatly\nreduced,\nso that the triaxial geometry\nis\nthe best choice\nfor the MAGSAT\nVector\nMagnetometer.\nThe\nbasic\nproblem\nwith\nthe\nsingle-axis\nsensor\nis the\nfact\nthat\nit has\nno\nfeedback\nfor\nfield\ncomponents\nperpendicular\nto its axis.\nIt seems\nintuitively\nobvious\nthat\nthis\ndifficulty\ncan\nbe corrected\nby use\nof a three\ndimensional\nfeedback\nfield,\nusing\nthree\northogonal\nsensors.\nThis\nsupposition\nis readily confirmed\nby analysis.\nConsider\nnow a vector\nequation\nfor the three sensor\noutputs\nBS\n\n= Rs(B\n\n+ B F)\n\n(I)\n\nAs before,\nB is the ambient\nfield and B F is the feedback\nfield, but R S is\nnow a 3 x 3 matrix\n(an orthogonal\nrotation matrix\nif all three sensor\nscale\nfactors are equal).\nAs before,\nthe feedback\nfield is determined\nby an equation\nof the form\nB F\n\n=\n\n-R F\n\nM\n\nBS\n\n(2)\n\nexcept\nthat RF\nand M are now\n3 x 3 matrices:\nR F is an orthogonal\nrotation\nmatrix,\ncorresponding\nto the misalignment\nof the feedback\ncoils, while M\nis a diagonal\nmatrix,\nwhose\ndiagonal\ncomponents\nare the three respective\nloop gains,\nwhich\nof course\nmay\ndiffer somewhat.\nThe telemetered\nfield\nis\n+\nB T\n\nwhile\nThis\n\nequation\n\nerror\n\n\xc3\xb7\nBS\n\n-1\n\nvector\nis solved\n\n=\n\n(I + M\n\n-R F\n\n\xc3\xb7\nB F\n\nis AB\n\n=\n\n= BT\n\n- B.\n\nRsRF)-I\n\nM\n\nB S and\n\nB T to obtain\n\nthe result\n\nRS B\n\n(4)\n\nfield is then\n\ngiven\n\nby\n\nl\n=\n\n(I + M\n\ninfinite loop\n\n*\nAB\n\n(3)\n\nby eliminating\n\nin the telemetered\n+\nAB\n\nFor\n\nM\n\nthe error\n\nB T\nThe\n\n=\n\ngain\n\n= RF-I(1\n\nRsRF)along\n\n- RF)\n\n[M\n\nRS(1\n\nall three\n\ng\n\n=\n\n(R fl\n\n- RE)\n\naxes,\n\n-\n\n- I] B\n\nthe result\n\n1)\n\n(5)\nis\n\n*\nB\n\nThis\nerror\nis proportional\nto the\ndifferences\nbetween\nthe feedback\ntion\nmatrix\nand the\nunit\nmatrix,\nwhich\nmeans\nthat\nmisalignments\nfeedback\ncoil\nby an angle\nA produce\nerror\nsignals\nin orthogonal\nof order\nB sin A.\n\n(6)\ncoil\nof the\nchannels\n\nThe\nerror\nis independent\nof sensor\nalignment\n(but\nnot sensor\noffset\nand\nnoise,\nof THE\n\nDesign\nConfiguration\n\nAnalysis\n\nFEEDBACK\n\nCOIL\n\nSPACING\n\nTO\n\nMINIMIZE\n\nCOIL\n\nSIZE\n\nThe uniformity\nof the field at the offset fluxgate sensor\ncan be improved\nby triaxial\nfeedsense\nto modify\nof the\nsensor\nrather\nbe used\nand\na\n\nlower\n\nweight\ncan be attained.\nAs noted\npreviously,\nthe\ncritical\ndirection\nfor\ntranslation\nis in the\ndirection\nof the\nexisting\nsensor\noffset.\nIn the\nother\ndirections\nthe\nsensor\nis symmetrically\nlocated,\nand translational\nmotions\ngive\nrise\nonly\nto very\nsmall\nsecond-order\nchanges\nin the\naverage\nfield.\nSingle-axis\nsensors\nsymmetrically\nlocated\nin fields\nof much\npoorer\nuniformity\nprovide\nadequate\nperformance\nwith\nrespect\nto sensor\ntranslation,\nso we expect\nno\nproblems\nwith\nmotion\nalong\nthe\ndirections\nin which\nthe\nfield\nis symmetric.\nThus,\nwe wish\nto make\nthe\nfield\nmore\nor less\nsymmetric\nin the\noffset\ndirection\nas well.\nThe\n\nactual\n\nway\n\nin which\n\nthe\n\nsensor\n\nresponds\n\nto\n\nthe\n\ndetails\n\nof the\n\nfield\n\nis very\ncomplicated.\nTo solve\nthe problem\nin one assumes\nconstant\npei\'meability\nin the\nsensor.\nA more\npractical\napproach\nis to adjust\nthe field\nfor a maximum\nat the\ncenter\nof the\nsensor\nfor\na first\napproximation\nand then\nto optimize\nthe\ncoil\nseparation\nexperimentally\nto yield\nzero\nfirst-order\ntolerance\nto sensor\nposition.\nThe\ndesign\nto be presented\nhas\nso much\nmargin\nsuch\nthat\nfurther\nopt[m[zatlon\nis\nprobably\nunnecessary.\nWe wish\nfirst\nto establish\nthe\nspacing\nwhich\nprovides\na suitable\nextremum\nin the field\nat the\noffset\nposition\nof the\nsensor.\nIf the\nvariation\nof the\nfield\naveraged\nover\nthe\nsensor\nis then\nsmall\nenough\nso that\nsensor\nmotion\ngives\nrise\nto an acceptably\nsmall\nchange\nin the\naverage\nfield,\nwe\ncan expect\nthat\nthe\nactual\nperformance\nwill\nalso\nbe acceptable.\nField\nCalculation\n- To evaluate\nthe\nvariation\nof the\nfield\nas a function\nof coil\nspacing,\nit Configuration\n\nDERIVATION\n\nOF\n\nSTRUCTURAL\n\nAnalysis\nSTABILITY\n\nREQUIREMENTS\n\nThe requirements\nfor structural\nstability follow from\nthe field equations.\nThe most\ncritical parameter\nis the coil alignment.\nThe dimensional\nstability required\nto ensure\nscale factor stability is equally critical.\nTo do the structural\nand thermal\ndesign,\nit is necessary\nto know\nthe\nsensitivity of the field to the coil parameters.\nThese\nsensitivities\ncan be\nreadily calculated\nfrom\nthe field equations\nor from\ngeometrical\nconsiderations.\nCoil Ali_nment\nStability - Misalignment\nof the magnetometer\ncan arise\nfrom\nstructural\nor thermal\ninstability of the feedback\ncoil orientations\nwith respect\nto each other or with respect\nto the alignment\nsurfaces;\nthe\ntotal angular\ninstability from\neither of these sources\nis not to exceed\n5 seconds\nof arc.\nThis requirement\nis very stringent,\nsince it corresponds\nto a dimensional\nchange\nof 25 ppm\n(25 microinches\nper inch).\nNote\nthat if one coil of a pair tilts with respect\nto the other, the net misalignment\nis half the tilt. Pincushion\nor other axially symmetric\ndistortion\nof\nthe coil will cause\na scale factor error\nbut not a misalignment.\nScale Factor\nStability - The required\nscale factor stability is equally\ndifficult to attain.\nOn the opposite\npage (Table\n4-12), the central field has\nbeen expressed\nin terms\nof the diameters\nand spacings\nof the inner and\nouter cancellation\ncoil pairs.\nBy differentiating\nthis formula,\none obtains\nthe sensitivity of the central field to changes\nin the dimensions.\nFor the\nnominal\ndesign\nin which\nboth the inner and outer cancellation\ncoils are\nHelmholtz\ncoil pairs,\nwith the outer coils having twice\ninner coils, the numerical\nvalues\nshown\nare obtained.\n\nthe diameter\nof the\nThe most\nsensitive\n\nparameter\nis the inner coil spacing,\nwhich\nproduces\na fractional field variation which\nis 24/35 the fractional\nvariation\nin the spacing.\nThe absolute\nsensitivity is 35Y]mil\nfor a l. ES-inch\nspacing.\nAtolerance\nof l. SYwas\nas signed to the feedback\ncoil constants\nin the error allocation presented\nearlier,\nor 23 ppm\nin terms\nof the 64000Y\nfull-scale field.\nAssuming\nthat\nthe structure\nexpands\nuniformly,\nthe overall sensitivity\nto thermal\nexpansion can be calculated\nby adding\nthe coefficients\nopposite\nalgebraically.\nThe result is unity (35/35) so that the regional\nstructural\ndimensional\nstability is 23 ppm-about equal to the requirement\nfor alignment\nstability.\nFluxgate\nTranslation\nand Orientation\n- Errors\nfrom\nthese sources\nare\ncontrolled\nby triaxial feedback\nwith proper\nshaping\nof the feedback\nfield,\nas explained\nin detail previously.\nThe field has been designed\nto produce\nacceptable\nscale factor stability and alignment\nif the fluxgate position is\nstable to 0.001\ninch and the orientation\nis stable to 1 milliradian.\nThese\nrequirements\nare summarized\nments\nare given in the table;\ndetails, since the coil system\n\n4-26\n\nin Table\n4-13.\nOnly\nthe mechanical\ndesign\nmay\nvery well expand\n\nthe overall requiremust\nconsider\nother\nnon-uniformly\n(distort).\n\n"rIME-ZERO\n\nTABLE\n\n4-12.\n\nSENSITIVITY\n\nOF\n\nTHE\n\nFIELD\n\nTO\n\nDIMENSIONAL\n\nThese\nformulas\ngive\nthe\ntolerances\nthermal\ndesign.\nNumerical\nvalues\nequal\nto their\nradius,\nand that\nthe\neter\nof the\ninner\ncoils.\n\nwhich\nmust\nbe met\nby\nassume\nboth\ncoil\npairs\nouter\ncancellation\ncoils\n\nExpression\n\n(SI\n\nFor\n\nthe\n\nCentral\n\nField\nd 1\n\nVARIATIONS\n\nthe\nstructural\nhave\na spacing\nare\ntwice\nthe\n\nand\ndiam-\n\nUnits)\nN 2\n\nd2\n\n_oN11Q\nd\n\n1\n\nSymbols\nd 1\n\n=\n\ninner\n\ncoil\n\ndiameter\n\ns 1\n\n= inner\n\ncoil\n\nspacing\n\ndz\n\n=\n\ncoil\n\ndiameter\n\nouter\n\nSensitivity\n\n(N2/N\n\n=\n\n1)\n\ncoil\n\nIn\n\n_B\n\nTerms\n\nOf\n\n1 2 dl3\n\n=\n\nCentral\n\nspacing\n\nouter/inner\n\nQ = shape\n\nFormulas\n\ndl\n\n= outer\n\ns2\n\ncoil\nfactor\n\nturns\n\n= 7/8\n\nratio\n\n= O. Z - Sensor\nOF\n\nTHE\n\nSENSOR\n\nThe\nsensor\nstability\nfeedback\ncoils\non the\ncoil\npower\nlow\nenough\n\nDesign\nFOR\n\nrequirements\nspherical\nto reduce\n\nand\n\nPerformance\n\nHIGH\n\nAnalysis\n\nSTABILITY\n\ncan\nbe exceeded\ngraphite\nepoxy\nforms\nthe\nthermal\neffects.\n\nby\n\nwinding\nand\nby\n\nthe\nkeeping\n\ntriaxialthe\n\nThe\ndesign\nof the\nsensor\ndepends\non a combination\nof magnetic,\nthermal,\nand mechanical\nfactors.\nAfter\nso much\nanalysis\nit may\nbe helpful\nto\nreview\nthe\noverall\ndesign\napproach\nby way\nof a summary.\nAs indicated\npreviously,\nour\nanalysis\nand that\nof others\nshows\nthat\nhigh\naxial\nstability\nis much\nmore\neasily\nattained\nif the\nthree\nfluxgate\nsensors\nare\nenclosed\nin\na single\ntriaxial\n(vector)\nfeedback\nfield,\nrather\nthan\nbeing\nenclosed\nin\nthree\nseparate\nsingle-axis\nfeedback\nsolenoids.\nA detailed\nanalysis\nof the\ntriaxial\nfeedback\nscheme\nand a comparison\nof triaxial\nand\nsingle\naxis\nfeedback\nhas\nbeen\npresented.\nThe\nprincipal\nerror\nsource\nin the\nsingle-axis\nsystem\nis the\ninstability\nof alignment\nof the\nsensitive\ncore;\nthis\nsensitivity\nis reduced\nby a large\nfactor\nbytriaxial\nfeedback.\nOther\nerrors,\nsuch\nas\nthe\naxial\ninstability\nof the\nfeedback\ncoils,\nare\ncomparable\nfor\neither\nsystem.\nDesign\nof Feedback\nCoil/Sensor\nSystem\n- If the\nfield\ninside\nthe\ntriaxial\nfeedback\ncoils\nwere\nperfectly\nuniform,\nthe\nposition\nand\norientation\nof the\nsensors\nwould\nbe almost\nirrelevant.\nWe have\nselected\nthe\nsimplest\nfeedback\ncoil\nsystem\nwhich\nproduces\nadequat\ne uniformity\nfor\nring-core\nsensors\nlarge\nenough\n(3/8\ninch,\nor about\n1 cm,\nin diameter)\nto meet\nthe\nnoise\nspecification-namely,\na Helmholtz\ncoil\npair\nalong\neach\naxis.\nA\nlarger\npair\nis used\nto cancel\nthe\nexternal\nfield,\nas discussed\npreviously\nand\nshown\nin the\nfigure\nopposite.\nThe\nring-core\nfluxgate\nsensors\nare\nmounted\northogonally\non a cube.\nThey\nare\nmade\nas small\nas possible\nconsistent\nwith\nmeeting\nthe\nnoise\nspecification.\nTheir\ndimensions\nwere\nadjusted\nto minimize\nthe\nnoiseequivalent\nfield\nsubject\nto the\ngeometric\nsize\nconstraint.\nThe\ninner\nfeedback\ncoils\nare\npushed\ntogether\nslightly\nto make\nthe\nfield\nflat\nat the\nsensors\nrather\nthan\nat the geometric\ncenter\nof the\ncoils.\nMechanical\nand\nThermal\nDesign\nof the\nSensor\nAssembly\n- The\nprimary\nconsideration\nin the\ndesign\nof the\nsensor\nassembly\nis mechanical\nand\nthermal\nstability\nof the\nfeedback\ncoils,\nwhich\nis the\nmain\nfactor\nin determining\nthe\ngain,\nlinearity,\nand\nalignment\nstability\nof the\ninstrument.\nIt has\nbeen\ndetermined\nthat\na graphite-fiber\nepoxy-resin\nmaterial\nwill\nprovide\nthe\nrequired\nmechanical\nand thermal\nstability.\nThe\nsensor\nassembly\nis composed\nof a base,\na sensor\ntower,\nand two\nspheres\nof graphite-epoxy\non which\nthe\ncoils\nare\nwound.\nIn order\nto\nachieve\nthermal\nstability,\na thermal\nresistance\nand\ncoil\npower\nmust\nbe\nselected\nthat\nwill\nresult\nin an acceptable\nthermally\ninduced\nvariation\nin the\nfeedback\nfield.\nThe\nproposed\ndesign\nproduces\na thermal\nvariation\nof the\nfield\nof less\nthan\n0. l\'/with\na coil\npower\nof 20 roW.\nRejection\nof Thermal\nGradients\n- The\nsensor\nenclosure\nshould\nbe isothermal,\nsince\ngradients\nof I\xc2\xb0C\nlead\nto field\nvariations\nin the\n0. 1V region\n(because\nof Sensor\nDesign\nSTRATEGY\n\nFOR\n\nCONTROLLING\n\nand\n\nPerformance\n\nTHERMAL\n\nAnalysis\nEFFECTS\n\nMean\ntemperature\nvariations\nare reduced\nby use of active temperature\ncontrol, while the effects of gradients\nare eliminated\nby the use of isotropic\nstructural\nmaterial,\nthermal\ninsulation,\nand a thermally\nconductive\nstructure\n\nwith\n\nlow\n\ninternal\n\npower\n\ndissipation.\n\nTo provide\nthe absolute\naccuracy\nand\nalignment\nstability\nrequired\nfor\nMAGSAT,\nit is necessary\nto avoid\nthermal\nexpansion\nof the\nfeedback\ncoils,\nparticularly\ndistortions\narising\nfrom\nunequal\nexpansion\nof different\nparts\nof the\nstructure.\nEven\nif the\nstructure\nis monolithic,\nso that\nall parts\nof\nit have\nthe\nsame\nexpansion\ncoefficient,\nsuch\ndifferential\nexpansions\ncan\nresult\nfrom\ntemperature\ngradients\nin the\nstructure.\nNeed\nfor\nActive\nTemperature\nControl\n- Even\nwhen\nthermally\nstable\nstructural\nmaterials\nare\nused,\nthere\nis still\na requirement\nfor\ntemperature\ncontrol.\nThe\noverall\ntemperature\ncoefficient\nof the coil\nstructure\nwill\nhave\na non-zero\nthermal\nexpansion\ncoefficient\nbecause\nof an imperfect\nmatch\nbetween\nthe thermal\nexpansion\nof the copper\nand\nthat\nof the\ncoil\nforms;\nwe\nestimate\nthat\nthe\ncoefficient\ncould\nbe as large\nas 2 ppm/\xc2\xb0C,\nleading\nto a\nfield\ntemperature\ncoefficient\nsomewhere\nbetween\n1 and 2 ppm/\xc2\xb0C\nby our\nprevious\nsensitivity\nanalysis.\nBecause\nan overall\nstability\nof about\n20 ppm\nis needed,\nwith\nerrors\narising\nfrom\nseveral\nadditional\nsources,\nmean\ntemperature\ncontrol\nto about\n+l\xc2\xb0C\nis desirable.\nSeveral\nmethods\nof achieving\nthis\ncontrol\nwere\nconsidered;\nas discussed\nlater,\nit appears\nthat\nan electrical\n\nheating\nscheme\nfits\nthe\nrequirements\nbest.\nMaterial\nSelection\n- The\ngraphite-epoxy\nmaterial\nrecommended\nhas\ntwo\nvirtues:\nvery\nhigh\nelastic\nmodulus\nand\nhence\nhigh\nrigidity,\nand high\nthermal\nconductivity\n- much\nhigher\nthan\nthat\nof most\nplastics\nand\nat best\ncomparable\nto such\nmetals\nas titanium.\nHowever,\nthis\nmaterial\nis often\nfurnished\nas a laminate\nhaving\nhigh\nelastic\nand thermal\nconductivity\nonly\nin\nthe\nplane\nof the\nlaminations.\nUse\nof such\nan anisotropic\nmaterial\nfor\nthe\ncoil\nforms\nand\nsupports\nmight\nlead\nto trouble\nas a result\nof unequal\nthermal\nexpansion\nin different\ndirections.\nFor\nthis\nreason,\nthe\nrecommended\nmaterial\nis isotropic\nwith\nrandomly-oriented\ngraphite\nfibers.\nShielding\nfor\nElimination\nof Temperature\nGradients\n- Temperature\ngradients\narise\nfrom\nthe\nheating\nof the\nmagnetometer\nby the\nsun on one\nside\nand by cooling\nto space\non the\nother\nside,\nas well\nas from\nself-heating\nof the\ncoils\nand\nsensors.\nThe\nelimination\nof gradients\nimplies\nthat\nthe thermal\nmodel\nof the\nimportant\nparts\nof the\ninstrument\n- namely\nthe\nfeedback\ncoil\nstructure\nand\nbaseplate\n- should\nbe represented\nto a high\ndegree\nof accuracy\nas a single\nthermal\nnode.\nThis\nrequirement\nimplies\ncareful\ninsulation\nof this\nnode\nfrom\nexternal\ninfluences,\nthe\nuse\nof a highly\nconductive\nstructure,\nand the\navoidance\nof self-heating\nby keeping\nthe coil\npower\ninput\nlow.\nAll of these\nrequirements\nare\nmet\nby the design.\nSolar\nHeating\nEffect\n- The\norientation\nof the\ninstrument\nand\nsatellite\nin\norbit\nis indicated\nin Figure\n4-16.\nIn the\nnominal\nnear\npolar\norbit,\none\nside\nof the\ninstrument\nwill\nbe continuously\nilluminated\nby the\nsun,\nwhile\nthe\nother\nside\nwill\nbe continuously\nexposed\nto space\n(the\neclipse\ncase\nis discussed\nlater).\nBy using\na surface\ncoating\nwitha\nlov_ solar\nabsorptivity\nand\nhigh\nemissivity\non the\nsun\nside\n(e.g.,\nwhite\npaint),\nand\n(if possible)\na surface\nwith\na low\nemissivity\non the\nspace\nside,\nthe\ntemperature\ngradient\nacross\nthe\ninstrument\ncan\nbe minimized.\nThen,\na superinsulation\nand\na\nconductive\nhousing\nand coil\nstructure\ncan\nprovide\nthe\nrest\nof the\nisolation\nrequired.\n4-40\n\nTIME\n\n- ZEPlD\n\nThe\nmain\neffects\nthen\nbecome\nheat\nlosses\nfromthe\nfirst-surface\nalignment\nmirrors\nmounted\non the\nbaseplate\nand\nlosses\nto the\nuncontrolled\ninstrument\nmounting\nshelf.\nGradients\nproduced\nby this\ncooling\neffect\ncan\nbe reduced\nby\napplying\nheat\nbehind\nthe\nmirrors\nusing\nan appropriate\nprinted-circuit\nheater,\nand\nby isolating\nthe\nbaseplate\nfrom\nthe\ninstrument\nmount.\nThis\nthermal\ndesign\nis discussed\nin more\ndetail\nlater.\nSelf-Heating\n- Sensor\nDesign\nDESIGN\n\nOF\n\nTHE\n\nTHERMAL\n\nand\n\nPerformance\n\nCONTROL\n\nAnalysis\n\nSYSTEM\n\nA combination\nactive/passive\nthermal\ncontrol\nsystem\nheat interchange\nwith the sensor\nfeedback\ncoils.\n\nprevents\n\nexcessive\n\nThe thermal\ninterchange\nbetween\nthe sensor\nand its external\nenvironment\nmust\nbe minimized\nto keep misalignment\nand gain errors\nwithin limits.\nThe\nmajor\nproblem\nis heating by the sun on one side and cooling\nto space on the\nother side.\nTo stay within the errorallocations\nspecified,\nthe design must\ninclude the following\nfeatures:\nSuperinsulation\n- This recommended\ninsulation\nis actually multilayer\naluminized\nor goldized\nmylar\nor kapton.\nThe purpose\nof the insulation\nis to\nprovide\na very high thermal\nresistance\npath from\nthe external\nenvironment\ninputs (solar and space\nshadow)\nto the sensor\nfield cancellation\ncoils and\nfeedback\ncoils.\nThe insulation is about 0.5 inch thick and wit1 be placed\non\nthe outside of the sensor\nand in the space between\nthe field cancellation\ncoil\nand the thermal\nshunt.\nThe insulation is specially designed\nfor spherical shape to avoid the wrinkling\neffect obtained\nif a flat shape\nis wrapped\naround\na sphere.\nThe outer surface,\non the sun side, is painted white\nto reduce\nthe temperature\ndifference\nacross\nthe instrument.\nIf the orientation can be guaranteed,\nthe finish on the space\nside should be gold or aluminum.\nIf no such guarantee\nis possible,\npainting th entire outside\nsurface white is acceptable.\nThermal\nShunt - The\nthermal\nshunt is a graphite-fiber\nepoxy-resin\nsphere.\nThe principal\npurpose\nof the shunt is to equalize\nthermal\ninputs to\nthe coil portions\nof the sensor.\nThis is possible\nbecause\nthe shunt\nprovides\na good heat conduction\npath so that the temperature\ngradient\nacross\nthe\nshunt is minimized.\nA thermal\ncontrol\nfinish is applied\nto the exterior\nof\nthe shunt.\nBase and Mirror\nShield - The mirror\nand part of the sensor\nbase\nshould not be covered\nby the superinsulation\nfor obvious\nreasons.\nThe mirrors\nmust\nbe exposed\nfor alignment\nby a spacecraft\nlight source\nand the base\nmust\ninterface with the boom.\nThe rest of the base plate is covered\nby\nsuperinsulation.\nTo minmize\nsun and shadow\nradiative heat transfer,\na\nshield is provided\nto limit the field of view to primarily\nthe spacecraft.\nThermal\ninsulation between\nthe sensor\nand boom\ninterface will minimize\nconduction\nheat transfer.\nIt is recommended\nthat the portion of the boom\ninterface with the sensor\nalso be insulated and that the boom\nthermal\nconductive area be small.\nBase Heating\n- Because\nthe passive\nthermal\nprotection\nprovided\nby\nthe superinsulation\nand thermal\nshunt is only partially available\nat the base,\nactive thermal\ncontrol\nis used (see next topic for design\nof thermal\ncontroller).\nThe mirrors\nwill lose heat by radiation and hence\nan active heating element\nis necessary.\nA printed circuit type film heater\nand temperature\nsensors\nattached\nto the sensor\nbase can provide\nthe required\nbase\ntemperature.\n(Other\nheaters\nattached\nto the thermal\nshunt can be used to\nreduce\nthe gradients\neven further.)\nPerformance\n- The multiple-layer\napproach\nattenuates\nthe solar flux\nso that the direct effect on the feedback\ncoils is negligible.\nThe main\nsource\nof temperature\ngradients\nthen results from\nheat flux on the highly\nconductive\nbase plate, as we will now\nsee.\n/\n\n4 -44\n\nTIME-ZEI_D\n\nThe\nfirst-surface\nmirror\nlosses\nare a potentially\nserious\nsource\nof loss\neven\nthough\nits\nemissivity\nis low-100 mW for\na 10 cm x 10 cm mirror\nwith\nan emissivity\nof 0.02.\nBy placing\nthe\nheater\nbehind\nthe mirror,\nthe\nunbalanced\nheat\nflux\ndue to this\nconcentrated\nsource\nof - Sensor\nDesign\nSubsection\n4. 7 _ Sensor\nDesign\nDESIGN\nUse\n\nOF\n\nTHE\n\nof a printed\n\nTHERMAL\ncircuit\n\nheater\n\nand\n\nPerformance\n\nAnalysis\n\nCONTROLLER\nis recommended\n\nto warm\n\nbaseplate.\nThe heater\nshould be designed\nfor low stray\nby an ac current,\nusing a thermistor\nsensor\nand control\nvide mean\ntemperature\ncontrol to \xc2\xb1l\xc2\xb0C.\n\nthe instrument\nfields and\namplifier\n\ndriven\nto pro-\n\nTemperature\ncontrol of the sensor\nis needed\nto prevent\nvariation\nof the\nscale factor as well as instability of the sensor\naxis alignment.\nThe control requirement\nis about el\xc2\xb0C,\nalthough\none should\nbe able to do better\nthan that without much\ntrouble.\nSelection\nof Temperature\nControl\nScheme\n- Three\ndifferent control\nschemes\nwere\nconsideredgas flow, passive\ncontrol by a moving\nlouver,\nand electrical heating.\nThe gas flow method,\nusing cooling and heating\nof\ngas piped up the boom,\nwas\nrejected\nbecause\nit was\ndifficult to insulate the\ngas-carrying\ntubes.\nThe use of a thermostatic\nmechanism\nto control\na\nmoving\nlouver\nis an attractive alternative,\nbut the best place to locate such\na mechanism\nis on the baseplate,\nwhich\nis reserved\nfor alignment\nmirrors.\nAs discussed\npreviously,\naprincipal\nmode\nof heat loss is radiation\nfrom\nthe alignment\nmirror\nsurfaces.\nIt makes\nsense to distribute heat behind\nthe\nmirrors,\nin effect guarding\nthem\nand eliminating\nthe gradients\nwhich\nthe\nconcentrated\nload would\notherwise\nproduce\nin the baseplate.\nThis uniform\nheat distribution\ncan most\neffectively be provided\nby use of a printed\ncircuit heater.\nAvoiding\nMagnetic\nFields\n- Use\nof a dc heater\ndrive would\nobviously\nbe\nasking\nfor trouble,\nbecause\nof the stray fields that might\nbe produced.\nAn\nac drive should\nbe used,\nat a frequency\nwhich\nis midway\n(geometric\nmean)\nbetween\nthe 25-Hz\nlow frequency\nresponse\nand the 10-kHz\ndrive frequency-or about\nI kHz.\nUse\nof such an ac drive does not guarantee\nlack of stray field effects,\nbecause\nthe sensor\nis after all a highly non-linear\ndevice\nand crossmodulation\nproducts\nmay\nresult if the stray field is too large, whether\nit is\nac or not. To reduce\nthe stray field of the heater,\nit should\nbe laid out using\na bifllar pattern\nwith high spatial frequencies\nin two dimensions.\nThe formula\nopposite\ngives the spatial dependence\nof the vector potential produced\nby a current\ndistribution\nperiodic\nin the x-y plane.\nTo satisfy\nthe vector\nLaplace\nequation,\nthe fall-off of the z direction\nmust\nbe exponential. One readily estimates\nfrom\nthis formula\nthat if the printed\ncircuit\nconductor\nspacing\nis periodic\nwith a typical easily-attained\nspacing\nsI2 = 0. 050 inch, the field at the sensor\nlocation\n(7.5 inches\naway)\nwill be\nless than the field near the heater\nby a very large factor (I077).\nThe field\nproduced\nby such a periodic\nconductor\nlayout will thus be very small.\nThe\nprimary\nsource\nof stray field will be the dipole field produced\nby unavoidable current\nloops occurring\nwhere\nconnections\nare made;\nestimates\nof\nthese stray fields lead to field strengths\nof 0.2_\nat the sensors.\nSuch a\nfield strength\nis acceptable,\nespecially\nfor ac fields, so we conclude\nthat\na bifilar pattern\nheater\nwill indeed\nwork.\nController\nDesign\n- The design\nof the control\ncircuit\nand so has not been worked\nout in detail.\nUse\nof a GSFC\nis proposed\nfor the sensor.\n\nis straightforward\nPPLthermistor\n\nIt is recommended\nthat the controller\nbe a variable\nduty-cycle\ntype to\nachieve\nefficient operation\nat constant\nfrequency.\nThe heater\ncan be\nswitched\ndirectly across\nthe spacecraft\nsupply with a switch\nconduction\ninterval determined\nby the controller\nerror\nsignal.\nChokes\nin series with\n\n4-46\n\nTIME-ZEFI\xc2\xa3_\n\ni\n\nthe\nline\nand load\ncan\nbe used\nto times\ngreater\nfor the two-loop\nsystem.\nNoise\nConsiderations\n- The two-loop\nsystem\ncan accept\nsystemic\nnoise\nin the wide\nbandwidth\nloop of more\nthan ten times\nthat of the single-loop\nsystem.\nThis\nis a distinct\nadvantage\nduring\nimplementation\nwhen\ndealing\nwith digital\ntransients,\npower\nsupply\nnoise,\nspacecraft\ninterference,\nand all\nthe other\nSources\nof noise\nwhich\nare always\npresenf_nd\nn6t usually\namenable to analysis.\nOuter\nLoop\n- The outer\nloop,\nor OFG,\nmust\nprovide\nthe additional\ndynamic\nrange\nto allow\nthe two-loop\nsystem\nto operate\nover\nthe specified\nrange\nof a:64,000Y.\nIt accomplishes\nthis\nby sampling\nthe converted\ndigital\noutput\nof the inner\nloop to determine\nwhether\nit is within\neither\nthe bottom\nor top one-eighth\nof full scale\n(or in between)\nat a sample\nrate\nof approximately\n0.5 Hz.\nIf within\neither\nof the outer\noctants,\nthe sample\npulse\neither\nincrements\nor decrements\na six-hit\nreversible\ncounter\nin the OFG\nlogic.\nIf within\nthe interior\n75 percent\nof the ADC range,\nthe counter\nstate\nis not changed.\nThe output\nof the reversible\ncounter\nis input to a six-bit\nDAC where\nthe\noutput\nis converted\nto a feedback\ncurrent\nin the current\ngenerator.\nThe system\nparameters\nare selected\nso that each\nstep of the OFG is\nequivalent\nto Z500_/.\nThus,\nafter\neach\nincrement,\nahysteresis\nof approximately\n500Y exists\nto ensure\nthat the occurrence\nof OFG step\nchanges\nis\nminimized.\nTypical\ninput/output\ncurves\nfor increasing\nand decreasing\ninputs\nare\nshown\nin Figure\n5-5.\nAn obvious\nsecondary\nadvantage\nof this two-loop\nsystem\nis that a cross\ncalibration\nbetween\nthe ADC and the OFG is provided.\nOperating\nRange\n- With the selected\nparameters,\nthis\nsystem\nis capable\nof operating\nover\na range\nof -80,000Y\nto +81,5003t;\nhowever,\nif desired,\nthe\nlogic\ncould\nlimit\nthe up/down\ncounter\nrange\nto a limit\nof approximately\n+64,000Y.\nSummary\n- We have now described\nthe general\ncharacteristics\nof the\nsingle\nand the two-loop\nsystems,\nwhich\nshow that each\nhas its advantages\nand disadvantages.\nFurther\nanalysis\nof frequency\ncharacteristics\nand\nerrors\nfor a might\nappear\nthat the data requirements\nof the\ntwo-loop\nsystem\n(12 + 6 bits) are greater\nthan that required\nfor a singleloop system\nwith the same\nresolution\n(17 bits); however,\nthe six-bit DAC\nneed only be sampled\nfor incrementing\nand read out approximately\nonce\nevery\ntwo seconds,\nassuming\na maximum\ninput rate of 200 Y/second.\nThus,\nif the desired\nsampling\nrate were\n8 samples\nper second,\nthe single-loop\nsystem\nwould\nrequire\n8 x 17 = 136 BPS\nwhile the two-loop\nsystem\nwould\nneed only 8 x 12 + 6/2 = 99 BPS.\nThis is a significant\nsaving in telemetry\nspace\nand an additional argument\nfor the two-loop\nsystem.\n\n)\n\n5-1Z\n\nTIME*ZEFIQ\n\nTABLE\n\n5-4.\n\nSUMMARY\n\nOF\n\nTWO-LOOP\n\nSYSTEM\n\nAll error\nbudgets\ncan be met with Electronics Design\nSubsection 5.2 - Electronics Design and Performance Analysis\nDESIGN OF THE REFERENCE GENERATOR AND THE PROBE DRIVE\nThe\nrecommended\ndigital\ncount-down\nprovides\n\nhigh\n\nprobe\nchain\nefficiency\n\ndrive\ncircuit\nand\nreference\n\nuses\nphase\n\na crystal\nadjustment.\n\noscillator\nThe\n\nwith\nprobe\n\na\ndrive\n\noperation.\n\nThe probe\ndrive circuit and reference\ngenerator\nwere\ndetermined\nto be\nareas\nwhere\nhigh confidence\nin many\nproven\nsolutions\nexisted.\nThe probe\ndesign\ncalls for an excitation\nfrequency\nof 10 kHz,\nwhich\nis comparable\nto\nmany\nexisting designs.\nRequirements\n- The general\nrequirements\nof this subsystem\ninclude\ngood frequency\nstability, easy phase\nadjustment\nbetween\nthe probe\ndrive\nand the demodulator,\n2fo, reference\nsignal, and an efficient probe\ndrive\nwith good symmetry\nto minimize\neven harmonics.\nA Solution - The schematic\nof Figure\n5-6 shows\none method\nfor generating the probe\ndrive signal and the demodulator\nreference\nvoltage which\nmeets\nthese requirements.\nAs shown,\na 2-MHz\ncrystal\noscillator is used to generate\na stable frequency.\nIts output is counted\ndown\nin devices\nwhich\nprovide\ndecoded\ndecimal\noutputs.\nProper\nselection\nof one of the R lines and one of the C lines\nenables\nsetting the relative phases\nof drive and reference\nsignals to about\ntwo degrees.\nThe properly\nphased\nsignals from\nthe countdown\nchain are\ndivided once more\nto generate\nthe probe\ndrive reference.\nThe circuit used to generate\nthe probe\ndrive current\nis one which\nhas\nbeen used with the MJS\nSpacecraft\nMagnetometer\nSystem\ndescribed\nby\nM. Acuna*,\nand is frequently\nused to drive magnetic\namplifiers.\nThis\ncircuit has the advantage\nof providing\na large ratio of peak-to-average\ncurrent\nresulting from\nthe discharge\nof the capacitor\ninto the core when\nit saturates;\nit exhibits high efficiency\nbecause\nthe drive circuit supplies\nonly circuit losses.\nThe nonlinear\nresonant\ncircuit provides\nenergy\nstorage.\nThe digital drive generator\nhas the advantage\nthat the required\nodd\nsymmetry\nof the square\nwave\nvoltage\nis easily accomplished\nat these frequencies\nwith CMOS\nlogic elements.\nRedundancy\n- It is planned\nthat each of the three axes will have identical circuit boards,\nincluding the reference\ngenerators.\nAdditional\nstudies\nshould\nbe performed\non the total system\nreliability to determine\nthe best way of using the available\nredundancy\nof the three oscillators.\nNext we describe\nthe second\nharmonic\namplifiers\nof the inner loop.\n\n::\'-M. was\nassumed\nthat\nthe\ntelemetry\ninterfaces\nwould\nbe typical\nof other\nspacecraft\nand\nthat\nthe\ndata\nwould\nnot have\nto be estimated\n0.7\nW of power.\nThe\ntemperature\ncontrol\nrequirements\nare\neasily\nmet\nsince\n+5\xc2\xb0C\nis sufficient.\nAn operating\ntemperature\nof +85\xc2\xb0C\nis assumed\nwith a basic construction\nconsisting\nof discrete elements\nmounted\non a hybrid\nsubstrate\nwhich,\nin turn, is mounted\nin a hermetically\nsealed,\nevacuated\nhousing\nto minimize\nheat leaks.\nLow\nVoltage\nPower\nSupply\n- Many\ndesigns\nare available\nto meet\nthe\nLVPS\nrequirements.\nThe LVPS\nshould use switching\ntechniques\nto provide\nefficiencies\nin the order\nof 75 percent.\nPost regulators\nare assumed\non\n\xc2\xb115 V analog\nlines to provide\nbetter than 0. 5 percent\nregulation.\nPower\nEstimate\n- Table\n5-7 shows\nthe NATURE\n\nCalibration\n\nOF\n\nTHE\n\nand\n\nAlignment\n\nCALIBRATION\n\nAND\n\nALIGNMENT\n\nPROBLEM\n\nThe total specified overall accuracy\nof 5\xc2\xa5 per vector field component\nfor\nthis instrument\nrequires\na stringent\nerror\nbudget\nlimiting the contribution\nof each of the many\npotential sources\nof error.\nWith individual\nsources\nnecessarily\nsmall r their accurate\ndetermination\nbecomes\ndifficult.\nThe projected\nperformance\nof this magnetometer\nsubstantially\nexceeds\nthat of previous\ndesigns\nin stability and accuracy\nof alignment\nof the magnetic axes.\nThis advance\nin the state of the art in magnetometers\nwill\nrequire\na commensurate\nadvance\nin the techniques\nand instrumentation\nused to characterize\nand calibrate\nsuch sensors.\nThe degree\nof precision\nsought\nin the determination\nof sensor\nparameters\nis in many\ncases\nas\ngreat or greater\nthan that of the available\nmeasuring\ninstruments.\nThe table opposite\nenumerates\nthe primary\nsensor\nparameters\nthat\nthe calibration\nprogram\nmust\ndetermine\nand the allowable\nerrors\nattributed\nto each of them\nexpressed\nin units of magnetic\nfield.\nOffset - The zero applied magnetic\nfield output of the sensor\nis called\noffset and its maximum\nvalue and drift per year is specified\nat 0.4Y.\nDue\nto the presence\nof the earthls magnetic\nfield, measurement\nof this parameter requires\nthe generation\nof an opposing\nvector field to obtain a fieldfree volume\nnear the sensor.\nSince any such cancellation\nprocedure\nis\nlikely to be imperfect,\na gimbal\nmount\nfor the sensor\nis also required\nto\nallow\n180-degree\nrotations\nto remove\nthe effects of any residual\nfields on\nthe measurement.\nNoise\n- The random\nfluctuations\nin output from\na sensor\nin a steady\nfield can readily\nbe measured\nfor a given bandwidth\nprovided\nthat a sufficiently quiet field environment\ncan be supplied.\nMeasurement\nof sensor\nnoise of 0.3Y will require\nan environment\nthat is an order of magnitude\n(0.03Y) quieter.\nThe earthls\nmagnetic\nfield variations\nrange\nin amplitude\nfrom\na fewY\nat periods\nof 10-50 seconds\nto _IY at periods\nof 2-8 seconds.\nA mu-metal\nflux tank can reduce\nambient\nfields by several\norders\nof magnitude; since variations\nscale the same\nway as amplitudes,\nadequately\nquiet fields can be achieved\nover periods\nof time of the order\nof\none minute.\nScale Factor\n- The magnitude\nof voltage output due to a magnetic\nfield\napplied parallel to a given sensor\naxis is subject to variation\nas a function\nof sensor\noperating\ntemperature.\nThe allowable\nerror\ndue to both initial\nuncertainty\nand stability over the operating\nenvironment\nis budgeted\nat\n2.6"/. Since the scale factor determination\ninvolves\nknowledge\nof an output\nvoltage\nrequired\n\nand a magnetic\nfield, both\naccuracy.\nFor\na maximum\n\nquantities\napplied\n\nmust\nfield\n\nbe measured\nof 6. 4 x 104_/\n\nto the\nthe\nbud-\n\ngeted\nerror\nrepresents\n20 ppmwhich,\nequally\ndistributed,\nallows\n10 ppm\nerrors\nfrom\neach\nsource.\nCurrently\nachievable\naccuracies\nin the fluxgate\nliterature,\nit is possible\nto make\nquantitative\nestimates\nof the\nsignal-to-noise\nratio\nfor\nring\ncore\nsensors.\nThe\nnoise equivalent\nfield strength\nvaries\ninversely\nas the square\nroot of the product\nof frequency\nand core volume.\nThe\nfluxgate\nliterature\ncontains\nno clear-cut\nanalysis\nof the signal-tonoise\nperformance\nfor\nfluxgate\nsensors.\nThis\nlack\nis apparently\ncaused\nby\nthe fact\nthat\nit is customary\nto cite\nan early\nwork\nby William\nand Noble\n(I)\non Barkhausen\nnoise\nwhich\ndoes\nnot predict\neffects\nof the\nobserved\nmagnitude.\nIn fact,\nrecent\nexplanations\nof Barkhausen\nnoise\ndo appear\nto predict\nthe observed\nfluxgate\nsignal-to-noise\nratio,\nespecially\nwhen\nvalues\nof the\ndemagnetizing\nfactor\nappropriate\nto the\ncylindrical\ngeometry\nare\nused.\nThe most\nauthoritative\nreview\nof Barkhausen\nnoise appears\nto be that\nof H.\nBittel,\nwho\nreviews\nearlier\nwork\non the\neffect.\nThe\nprincipal\nreason\nwhy the effect appears\nto be larger than at first thought is that the elementary magnetic\ndipoles\nin the material\nare not reversed\none by one but\nrather\nin clustered\ngroups\ncontaining\nup to 10 +17 elementary\ndipoles.\nThe\neffect of this clustering\nis to produce\nfewer but much\nlarger\nnoise pulses,\nwhich\ncauses\na much\nhigher\nnoise signal than that calculated\nby G. W.\nMcFarlane\nand reported\nby Williams\nand Noble.\nAs a simple\napproximation to a very complex\nphenomenon,\nBittel calculates\nthat the Barkhausen\nnoise energy\nis enhanced\nover the white noise expected\nfrom\nthe flipping\nof single dipoles by a factor porportional\nto ncVdls , where\nn c is the number of domains\ninteracting\nin a cluster,\nv d is the domain\nvolume,\nand Is\nis the saturation\nmagnetization\n(expressed\nin the same\nunits as B, so\nthat\n\nI s = Bs).\nThe\nwork\non which\nBittel\nbased\nhis\nreview\nwas\nperformed\non grainoriented\n3_/0 Si-Fe,\na very\nnoisy\nmaterial\nunsuitable\nfor\nfluxgates\n(but\nideal\nfor\nthe study\nof Barkhausen\nnoise).\nFortunately,\nT.\nHiguchi\n(6) has\n)erformed\nmeasurements\non a number\nof core materials\nused in magnetic\namplifiers\nand modulators,\nincluding\nSupermalloy\nand Mo-Permalloy\nas\nwell as grain-oriented\n3_0 Si-Fe.\nThe noise for Mo-Permalloy\nis about\n\n500 times\nless than it is for the 3_0 Si-Fe,\nwhich,\npaper,\nleads to a value of ncV d for Mo-PermaUoy\nfactor of Z5 x 104 than for the 3_0 Si-Fe materials.\n\ncomparin_\nwith Bittel\'s\nof 4 x 10-1Z,\nless by a\n\nOne may\nnow calculate the signal-to-noise\nratio expected\nin a fluxgate\nsensor.\nTo keep things simple,\nwe have assumed\nthat the sensor\npreamplifier is untuned\nso that all even harmonics\nare kept; in practice,\nthis procedure\nwould\nprobably\ngive rise to high order\nharmonic\nsensitivity\nand\nphase\ninstability,\nbut the signal-to-noise\nratio should\nnot be greatly\ndifferent from\nthat of a practical\nsystem.\nThe result, derived\nin detail in the subsequent\npages,\nis shown\nopposite.\nThe noise-equivalent\nmagnetic\nfield varies\ndirectly with the saturation field of the core and inversely\nwith the demagnetizing\nfactor and the\nsquare\nroot of the core\nvolume,\ndrive frequency,\nand integration\ntime.\nThis result checks\nquantitatively\nas wet1, predicting\nnoise levels of-0.04Y\nrms\nwith typical core geometries.\n(A slight over estimate\nklue to vai-ious\nsimplifications.\n)\n\n.A-Z\n\nTII_IE\n\n* ZEFID\n\nTHE\nNOISE\nEQUIVALENT\nFIELD\nFOR\nA FLUXGATE\nMAGNETOMETER\nThe\nnoise-equivalent\nby the\nfollowing\nPermalloy\nused\n\nmagnetic\nformula.\nThe\nby Higuchi.\n\nK\n_Bn\n\nfield\nvalue\n\nfluxgate\nis\n4 x 10 -12\n\napproximated\ncm -3 for\n\nVd\n\n= 2-_/V---_\n\nn\n\nfor\na ring-core\nof ncv d is about\n\nBs\n\n= cluster\n\nnumber\n\n= domain\n\nvolume\n\nc\n\nvd\nV\n\n= core\n\nf\nT\nB\n\nvolume\n\n= drive\n\nfrequency\n\n= integration\n\ntime\n\n= saturation\n\ns\nK\n\nfield\n\n= demagnetizing\n\nF.C.\n\nWilliams\n\n2.\n\nD.I.\nGordon,\nMagnetics,\n\nand\n\nS.W.\n\nNoble,\n\nR.H.\nLundsten,\nVol MAG-I,\n330\n\nD.I. a\nproperly\nconstructed\nfluxgate\nsensor\nis magnetostrictive.\nThe research\nconducted\nat the Naval\nOrdnance\nLaboratory\nin developing\nthe lunar surface magnetometer\nfor Apollo\nshowed\nthat the best offset performance\nwas\nattained by using as a core material\na permalloy\ncontaining\n6 percent\nmolybdenum\nand 81.3 percent\nnickel.\nFor this nickel concentration,\nthe\nlongitudinal\nmagnetostriction\nis zero 2.\nEven when\nsuch material\nis used,\nsome\nresidual\neffect may\nbe present,\nso it is important\nto understand\nhow\nthe offset is generated.\nWeiner\n8 has presented\na theory\nof the effect,\nassuming\nsinusoidal\nwaveforms\nand a particular\nshape\nfor the magnetostriction curve.\nWeiner\nalso presents\ndata showing\nthat the effect varies\nwith drive level, peaking\nif the core is driven\njust to saturation,\nand\nbecoming\nmuch\nsmaller\nif the core is overdriven.\nFor permalloys\nwhose\nnickel content is near 80%,\nthe magnetostricrive elongation\nis small until the material\nsaturates,\nwhen\nthe elongation\nincreases\nto the (small) saturation\nvalue k s . It seems\nreasonable\nto treat\nthe magnetostrictive\ncurve\nas a step onset at saturation\nthe flux and magnetostriction\nduring the cycle will vary\nin Figure\nB.\nThe voltage induced\nin the second-harmonic\npickup\ne\n\n=\n\ndB\nNA--_\n\ndA\n+ NB-_-\n\n(Figure\nsomewhat\n\nA).\nThen,\nas shown\n\ncoil is given\n\nby:\n(i)\n\n,\n\nwhere\nN is the number\nof turns on the pickup\ncoil, A is the core crosssectional\narea, and B is the field intensity.\nThe\nsecond\nterm\nis the\nd_rivative\nof the magnetostrictive\nflux change\nterm\nin Figure\nB.\nThe\nmagnetostrictive\npart of the voltage waveform\n(Figure\nC) consists\nof a\nseries\nof spikes\nat the second\nharmonic\nof the drive frequency.\nThe area of each spike is roughly\ngiven by\n\nedt\n\n=\n\nWhen\ndivided\nmagnetic\nfield\nBo\nwhere\n\nNB\n\nby the\nunits\n=\n\nd is the\n\nAA\n\n= NB s k s A\n\nsensitivity\nis\n\ncalculated\n\n(2)\nearlier,\n\nthe\n\noffset\n\nexpressed\n\nin\n\n1\nt\nk\nB -4 s\ns d\ncore\n\ndiameter\n\nand\n\nt is the tape\n\nthickness.\n\nThis\n\nformula\n\npredicts\nthat the offset is independent\nof tape height, a rough result because\nit is based on the infinite-cylinder\ncalculatio_\nof the demagnetizing\nfactor.\nFor d = 1 inch, t = 0. 0005 inch, k s = 5 x i0 -u (79%NiFe)\nand B s = 0. 8T,\nthe offset estimated\nfrom\nthis formula\nis 0.5_/ -- not far from\nwhat is\nobserved.\nThe effect is temperature-dependent\nwhich\npresumably\ngives\nrise to the observed\noffset instability of a few tenths of a gamma.\nWhen\nthe longitudinal\nmagnetostriction\nis reduced\nby use of the proper\nalloy, residual\nvolume\nmagnetostriction\nstill exists.\nThis effect is very\nsmall,\nabout 1 part in 108 for the typical sensor\ndrive conditions,\nand\nmay\n\nbe neglected.\nThus,\nto obtain a sensor\nwith stable offset characteristics,\nit is\nadvisable\nto use as a core material\na Ni-Fe-Mo\nalloy with 81.3%\nnickel.\nA,-10\n\nTIldE*\n\nZERD\ni\n\nLENGTH\nAL
